Part II: Instructions: Please rate the contractor on a scale of Excellent, Good, Neutral, and Poor. The following information should be
considered when rating the identified factors:



Excellent– Performance met all contract requirements and exceeded many to the customer’s benefit. Problems, if applicable, were negligible and
were resolved in a timely, highly effective manner.



Good– Performance met all contract requirements and exceeded some to the customer’s benefit. There were a few minor problems which the
contractor resolved in a timely, effective manner.



Neutral – Performance met contract requirements. There were some minor problems and corrective actions taken by the contractor were
satisfactory. This rating is also assigned when there is no record of past performance or the record is inconclusive.



Poor– Performance did not meet most contractual requirements. There were serious problems and the contractor’s corrective actions were
ineffective.

J-6 Attachment VI - SSA Accessibility Requirements to EIT Solutions


Applicability of SSA’s Accessibility Requirements to EIT Solutions


The Social Security Administration considers accessibility to Electronic and Information Technology, hereafter referred to as “EIT”, a priority
for all employees and external customers, including people with disabilities.  SSA requires that EIT procured, developed, maintained, or
utilized meets the accessibility requirements under Section 508 of the Rehabilitation Act of 1973, as amended, 29 U.S.C. § 794d and additional
agency specific accessibility requirements, hereafter referred to in total as “SSA’s Accessibility Requirements”.  This is to ensure the
accessibility of its programs and activities to people with disabilities, specifically its obligation to acquire accessible EIT.  The EIT
deliverables covered under SSA’s Accessibility Requirements include:

    • Any equipment or interconnected system or subsystems of equipment used in the creation, conversion, or duplication of data or information.
      The term EIT includes, but is not limited to, software applications and operating systems, telecommunications products, worldwide websites,
      video, multimedia, information kiosks, office equipment (e.g., desktops, copiers, fax machines, printers, and notebook computers), and
      electronic content.

    • Any EIT deliverables developed, procured, maintained, or used by agencies directly or used by a contractor under a contract with an agency
      that requires the use of such product, or requires the use to a significant extent, of such product in the performance of a service or the
      furnishing of a product.

    • The final delivered EIT products provided through custom development, installation, configuration, integration, and maintenance services.
The contractor’s response may include a single EIT product or service, or be comprised of multiple EIT products and services bundled together
(i.e. solution).   Within this document, the term “EIT solution” shall refer to both.   All technical requirements and functional performance
criteria that are associated with the checked sections below must be addressed. At a minimum, the contractor’s EIT solution shall conform to the
following checked requirements:


Applicable Section 508 Standards[1]

|            |1194.21 Software Applications and Operating Systems                                                      |
|            |1194.22 Web Information and Applications                                                                 |
|            |1194.23 Telecommunications                                                                               |
|            |1194.24 Video and Multimedia                                                                             |
|            |1194.25 Self-contained, Closed Products                                                                  |
|X           |1194.26 Desktop and Personal Computers                                                                   |
|            |1194.31 Functional Performance Criteria                                                                  |
|            |1194.41 Information and Documentation Support                                                            |


1194.26 Desktop and portable computers.

(a) All mechanically operated controls and keys shall comply with §1194.23 (k) (1) through (4).
(b) If a product utilizes touchscreens or touch-operated controls, an input method shall be provided that complies with §1194.23 (k) (1) through
(4).
(c) When biometric forms of user identification or control are used, an alternative form of identification or activation, which does not require
the user to possess particular biological characteristics, shall also be provided.
(d) Where provided, at least one of each type of expansion slots, ports and connectors shall comply with publicly available industry standards.

Definitions of additional agency specific accessibility requirements

|1.1         |Software Compatibility with Assistive Technology                                                                       |
|            |All IT software deliverables provided as part of the contractor’s solution must be compatible with:                    |
|            |JAWS screen reading software (Version 9.0);                                                                            |
|            |MAGIC screen magnification software (Version 11); and                                                                  |
|            |Dragon Naturally Speaking Professional voice recognition software (Version 9.5).                                       |
|            |“Software” includes, but is not limited to, any of the following which contain a user interface:  websites, interactive|
|            |web based applications, client server applications, desktop applications, mainframe applications, applets, middleware, |
|            |and drivers.                                                                                                           |
|            |“Compatible” means that the software shall fully conform to the applicable Section 508 standards when used with the    |
|            |assistive technology referenced above.  Alternative assistive technologies embedded within the software to achieve     |
|            |accessibility (i.e. screen reader, screen magnifier, voice recognition)                                                |
|            |shall not be accepted as a substitute for compatibility with SSA’s assistive technology environment.                   |
|            |If the contractor’s solution includes installing the product in the SSA environment, the contractor shall explicitly   |
|            |state that the software shall be installed in a manner that shall not reduce the level of conformance with SSA         |
|            |accessibility requirements that currently exists.                                                                      |
|            |For a complete description on the JAWS and MAGIC software packages, please refer to Freedom Scientific’s web site at   |
|            |www.FreedomScientific.com.  To obtain a 30/60 day version of the JAWS/MAGIC software for development and testing,      |
|            |please send contact information and the SSA procurement number (for verification) to Charles Madsen at:                |
|            |Cmadsen@FreedomScientific.com.                                                                                         |
|            |For a complete description on the Dragon Naturally Speaking software package, please refer to Nuance’s web site at     |
|            |http://www.nuance.com/naturallyspeaking.  To obtain a trial version of the Dragon Naturally Speaking software for      |
|            |development and testing, please send contact information and the SSA procurement number (for verification) to Tom      |
|            |Derrico at: tderrico@nuance.com.                                                                                       |
|1.2         |Documentation in Accessible Formats                                                                                    |
|            |Any form of documentation provided (i.e. training manual, user guides, embedded documents etc.), including any         |
|            |documentation deliverables required in the statement of work, shall be provided in a fully accessible format.          |
|            |The documents shall be provided in one of the following formats:  Text, RTF, Microsoft Word or HTML format , or        |
|            |properly “tagged” PDF,. Properly tagged PDF’s can be verified by using Adobe Acrobat’s Accessibility Checker.          |
|            |Documentation delivered in a manner that is interactive (e.g., table of contents, Index, Search, etc.) shall be        |
|            |keyboard navigable, move focus to selected items (or have a keyboard alternative) and be comparable in keyboard access |
|            |to mouse usage.  All images (especially screenshots and technical diagrams (which are the sole means for conveying     |
|            |instructions) should include alternative text explaining the image so that a person who is blind would understand the  |
|            |screenshot, chart, figure, etc.  Documentation shall include information on the accessibility features of the product. |
|            |If keyboard shortcuts are provided to allow access to program functionality, a list of the keyboard shortcuts shall be |
|            |provided.                                                                                                              |
|            |Documentation that is delivered in a video or multimedia publication shall comply with the Section 508 requirements    |
|            |detailed in 36 CFR part 1194.24 and the functional performance criteria detailed in 36 CFR 1194 Subpart C.   In        |
|            |addition, SSA requires conformance to SSA’s Accessibility Requirements for all video and multi-media deliverables.  SSA|
|            |does not accept text equivalents used to replace speech, and requires captions to be synchronized with speech.         |
|            |                                                                                                                       |
|            |                                                                                                                       |
|1.3         |Video and Sound Card Compatibility with Assistive Technology                                                           |
|            |Video and sound cards purchased separately for, or included with, any desktop or portable computer systems shall be    |
|            |compatible with the following Assistive Technologies:                                                                  |
|            |JAWS screen reading software (Version 9.0);                                                                            |
|            |MAGIC screen magnification software (Version 11); and                                                                  |
|            |Dragon Naturally Speaking Professional voice recognition software (Version 9.5).                                       |
|            |Compatibility shall be determined based on the video/and or sound card’s ability to function with all three assistive  |
|            |technology in a manner that does not degrade either the core functionality of the AT or the performance of the AT.     |
|            |For a listing of video and sound cards that are compatible with the JAWS and MAGIC software packages, please refer to  |
|            |Freedom Scientific’s web site at www.freedomscientific.com.                                                            |
|            |For a listing of video and sound cards that are compatible with Dragon Naturally Speaking Professional, please refer to|
|            |Nuance’s web site at www.nuance.com/naturallyspeaking.                                                                 |
|1.4         |Hardware Devices that Contain Digital Windows                                                                          |
|            |Any hardware device shall provide an audible response for information displayed in a visual only format (i.e. digital  |
|            |message window) either through software or firmware.                                                                   |
|            |Any hardware digital window that has the capability to magnify text shall do so for all screens either through software|
|            |or firmware.                                                                                                           |
|            |Any hardware digital window that has the capability to adjust contrast settings shall provide a range of contrast      |
|            |levels either through software or firmware.                                                                            |
|            |Any hardware digital window that has the capability to be tilted for better viewing angles shall provide a range of    |
|            |settings.                                                                                                              |
|            |If digital windows meet the above requirements through software residing on a computer workstation, the software must  |
|            |be “compatible” with                                                                                                   |
|            |JAWS screen reading software (Version 9.0);                                                                            |
|            |MAGIC screen magnification software (Version 11); and                                                                  |
|            |Dragon Naturally Speaking Professional voice recognition software (Version 9.5).                                       |
|            |                                                                                                                       |
|            |Compatibility shall be determined based on the video/and or sound card’s ability                                       |
|            |to function with all three assistive technology in a manner that does not degrade either the core functionality of the |
|            |AT or the performance of the AT.                                                                                       |
|1.5         |Technical Support and Assistance (Hotline)                                                                             |
|            |Any technical support, help desks, or other support services provided to SSA shall accommodate the communication needs |
|            |of end users with disabilities, and shall be provided in one or both of the following options.  If both options are    |
|            |provided, each must conform to the accessibility requirements.                                                         |
|            |A toll-free telephone number that is accessible to all Government help desk personnel.  This shall include the         |
|            |availability of TTY access for help desk personnel who may require assistance for the hearing-impaired. When this      |
|            |option is provided, it must be available during SSA working hours (i.e. between 6am Eastern and 6pm Pacific time).     |
|            |An internet-based web page that is accessible to all Government help desk personnel.  This web site shall meet all of  |
|            |the requirements of Section 508 1194.22.                                                                               |
|1.6         |Training                                                                                                               |
|            |All training materials provided to SSA must be in an accessible format.  In addition, training materials on the use of |
|            |the accessibility features of a product or service shall be provided.                                                  |
|1.7         |Installation, Configuration & Integration Services                                                                     |
|            |If the contractor provides installation, configuration and integration services for commercial EIT solutions or EIT    |
|            |solutions previously developed for other government entities, the contractor shall not install, configure or integrate |
|            |the EIT solution in a way that reduces the existing EIT solution’s level of conformance with SSA’s accessibility       |
|            |requirements at the time the contract is awarded.                                                                      |
|1.8         |Maintenance & Replacements                                                                                             |
|            |Any updates or replacements to EIT products provided to SSA pursuant to this contract shall be fully accessible with   |
|            |all applicable SSA’s accessibility requirements as described above.  At a minimum, any updates or replacements to any  |
|            |IT deliverables shall not result in a decrease in accessibility from the EIT solution being maintained or replaced.    |
|1.9         |Labor Hours                                                                                                            |
|            |If the anticipated labor hour deliverable is expected to involve tasks that relate to or require the use of E&IT,      |
|            |delivered labor hours shall include knowledge and capabilities necessary to conform to SSA’s Accessibility             |
|            |Requirements.                                                                                                          |
|1.10        |Equivalent Facilitation                                                                                                |
|            |When a deliverable does not directly conform to the SSA Accessibility Requirements, but provides substantially         |
|            |equivalent or greater access by meeting the functional performance criteria in Subpart C of the Section 508 Standards, |
|            |per Section 1194.31, then it is said to have provided Equivalent Facilitation.                                         |
|            |Any approach providing Equivalent Facilitation that serves as a replacement to the Assistive Technologies SSA employs  |
|            |(e.g. an external speech engine) shall NOT be considered as an acceptable approach to Equivalent Facilitation.  For any|
|            |approach meeting Section 508 Standards using Equivalent Facilitation, the contractor shall be held accountable for     |
|            |maintaining and updating the approach.                                                                                 |


Acceptance Criteria


SSA reserves the right to perform testing on a contractor’s EIT solution in order to validate that the contractor has installed, configured or
integrated the EIT solution in a way that does not reduce the level of conformance with SSA’s Accessibility Requirements.

SECTION B –  Supplies or services and prices /cost

B-1.0       General Information

      This is a Performance Based contract with provisions for firm-fixed price and minimal labor-hour  rates.   The  contract  life  is  a  base
      period of one-year with four (one-year) option periods and 2 (two) 1 (one-year) performance based incentive periods.   Local  Area  Network
      (LAN) relocation services are being procured on a fixed-price basis.  Miscellaneous Relocation Tasks (“tasks”) will  be  priced  using  the
      fixed loaded hourly rates provided in Attachment I-Pricing Tables.  Unit prices are provided for the base contract year and contract  years
      one (1) through seven (7).

      Services to be performed under this contract are to be performed by competent, experienced, and highly qualified  personnel.   For  pricing
      purposes service personnel are divided into two categories:


      Local Field Engineer:  the first level of relocations and task support.  The Local Field Engineer will assist  in  the  deinstallation  and
      reinstallation of LAN components, not involving a file server.


      Local Technical Specialist: the second level of relocation and task support.  The Local  Technical  Specialist  performs  reconfigurations,
      equipment setup, relocations involving a server.

B-2.0 Table B-1 Unit Pricing Table Instructions

      Section B-2.1 provides instructions for the Unit Pricing Tables in Attachment I – Pricing Tables, Table B-1.

      B-2.1 LAN Relocations – Deinstallation/ Reinstallation (Table B-1 LR01 – LR16)


           The following Item Numbers in  Table B-1 apply to LR01 – LR08 for 30+ day notice and LR09 to LR16 for 14 to 29 day notice.


           Table B-1 for Item Numbers LR01 – LR08, the fixed prices for LAN relocations.  Relocation  is  defined  as  the  de-installation  and
           reinstallation of a LAN (including all LAN connections) and bringing the LAN to an operational status.  All services shall be  priced
           on a fixed-price-per-LAN basis (not hourly rates), and shall include, but not be limited  to,  all  labor,  travel  costs,  material,
           parts, packaging, trash removal, other costs, overhead, G&A and profit.  Shipping costs and cabling  costs,  however,  are  excluded.
           The Government shall reimburse the Contractor the actual shipping cost incurred.  The shipping cost shall be a separate line item  on
           an invoice.  Shipping cost shall be limited to the costs for pick-up, transport and delivery from the  existing  location  to  a  new
           location, (different building).  Reimbursable shipping cost excludes preparation for shipment and unpackaging.   Cabling  effort,  if
           required, will be separately priced outside of the relocation unit price.


      B-2.2 Workstation Relocations-standalone workstations ( TABLE B-1 WR01)


           The following Item Numbers in Table B-1 apply to WR01.


           Workstation Relocations - the cost for standalone workstation relocations will be  based on a fixed unit price  per  workstation  and
           shall include but not be limited to all labor, travel costs, material, parts, packaging, overhead, G & A, and profit.  Shipping  cost
           however, shall be excluded.  The Government shall reimburse the Contractor the actual shipping  cost  incurred.   The  shipping  cost
           shall be a separate line item on an invoice.  Shipping costs shall be limited to the costs for pick-up, transport and  delivery  from
           the existing location to a new location, (different building).  Reimbursable shipping cost does not include preparation for  shipment
           and unpackaging.


      B-2.3 Miscellaneous Relocation Tasks Hourly Pricing (TABLE B-1 TO01 – TO04)


           The following Item Numbers in Table B-1 apply to TO01 – TO04.


           Tasks Unit Price - The Government, at its option, may require the  Contractor  to  perform  tasks  related  to  relocation,  such  as
           redressing of LAN cabinets and other tasks identified in Section C-3.3.  These tasks will be priced  using  the  fully  loaded  labor
           rates.

           Enter the fixed loaded hourly rates.  These rates are fully loaded and include travel, mileage, overhead, G&A, and profit.  The  cost
           for cable and other materials/supplies is not included and will be reimbursed only if pre-authorization is given  by  the  COTR.  The
           task order will be modified to include the additional cost.


           Please Note: A task, at the discretion of the Government, may include a not to exceed amount of $2,500  for  materials  and  supplies
           needed during the performance of that task.  In these cases, the Government will only pay for the cost of the materials and supplies.
            Overhead, G&A, and profit are not allowable costs.  Moreover, the Contractor must substantiate these material costs as part of their
           invoice.


           Services to be performed under this contract are to be performed by competent, experienced, and highly qualified personnel.


      B-2.4 Initial (NEW) LAN Installation During Normal And Outside Normal                                      Business Hours (TABLE B-1 ILI01-
      ILI16)








           The following Item Numbers in Table B-1 apply to Initial (NEW) LAN Installations during “Normal Business Hours”, ILI01 – ILI08.   The
           following Line Items apply to Initial (NEW) LAN Installations “Outside Normal Business Hours”, ILI09 –  ILI16.   Business  hours  are
           defined in Section C-2.1 Definitions.


           The fixed prices are provided for Initial LAN  Installations  during  normal  business  hours  and  outside  normal  business  hours.
           Installation is defined as the installation of a LAN using Government Furnished Equipment (GFE), (including all LAN connections)  and
           bringing the LAN to an Operational status.


      B-2.5 Emergency New LAN Installation During Normal – And Outside Normal Business Hours (TABLE B-1 ELI01-ELI16)


           The following Item Numbers in Table B-1 apply to Emergency New LAN Installation during “Normal Business Hours,” ELI01 –  ELI08.   The
           following Line Items apply to Emergency New LAN Installations “Outside Normal Business Hours,” ELI09 –  ELI16.   Business  hours  are
           defined in Section C-2.1, Definitions.


           The fixed prices are provided for EMERGENCY LAN Installations during  normal  business  hours  and  outside  normal  business  hours.
           Installation is defined as the installation of a LAN using Government Furnished Equipment (GFE), (including all LAN connections)  and
           bringing the LAN to an Operational status.



      B-2.6 LAN Relocations – Deinstallation/ Reinstallation including VOIP Phones   (Table B-2 LR01- LR09)


           The following Item Numbers in  Table B-2 apply to this section, LR01 – LR08 for 30+ day notice and LR09 to LR16  for  14  to  29  day
           notice.


           Table B-2 for Item Numbers LR01 – LR08, the fixed prices for LAN  relocations  are  provided.   Relocation  is  defined  as  the  de-
           installation and reinstallation of a LAN (including all LAN connections and VOIP telephony desktop equipment) and bringing the LAN to
           an operational status.  All services shall be priced on a fixed-price-per-LAN basis (not hourly rates), and shall include, but not be
           limited to, all labor, travel costs, material, parts, packaging, trash removal, other costs,  overhead,  G&A  and  profit.   Shipping
           costs and cabling costs, however, are excluded.  The Government shall reimburse the Contractor the  actual  shipping  cost  incurred.
           The shipping cost shall be a separate line item on an invoice.  Shipping cost shall be limited to the costs  for  pick-up,  transport
           and delivery from the existing location to a new location, (different building). Reimbursable shipping cost excludes preparation  for
           shipment and unpackaging.  Cabling effort, if required, will be separately priced outside of the relocation unit price.


      B-2.7 Workstation Relocations (Table B-2 WR01)


           The following Item Numbers in Table B-2, applies to this section, WR01.


           Workstation Relocations - the cost for standalone workstation relocations will be  based on a fixed unit price  per  workstation  and
           shall include but not be limited to all labor, travel costs, material, parts, packaging, overhead, G & A, and profit.  Shipping  cost
           however, shall be excluded.  The Government shall reimburse the Contractor the actual shipping  cost  incurred.   The  shipping  cost
           shall be a separate line item on an invoice.  Shipping costs shall be limited to the costs for pick-up, transport and  delivery  from
           the existing location to a new location, (different building).  Reimbursable shipping cost does not include preparation for  shipment
           and unpackaging.


      B-2.8 Miscellaneous Relocation Tasks Hourly Pricing (Table B-2 TO01-TO04)


           The following Item Numbers in Table B-2 apply to this section, TO01 – TO04.


           Tasks Unit Price - The Government, at its option, may require the  Contractor  to  perform  tasks  related  to  relocation,  such  as
           redressing of LAN cabinets and other tasks identified in Section C-3.3.  These tasks will be priced  using  the  fully  loaded  labor
           rates.

           Enter the fixed loaded hourly rates.  These rates are fully loaded and include travel, mileage, overhead, G&A, and profit.  The  cost
           for cable and other materials/supplies is not included and will be separately reimbursed.


           Please Note: A task, at the discretion of the Government, may include a not to exceed amount of $2,500  for  materials  and  supplies
           needed during the performance of that task.  In these cases, the Government will only pay for the cost of the materials and supplies.
            Overhead, G&A, and profit are not allowable costs.  Moreover, the Contractor must substantiate these material costs as part of their
           invoice.


           Services to be performed under this contract are to be performed by competent, experienced,  and  highly  qualified  personnel.   See
           Section C-2.0 for description of duties.


      B-2.9 Initial (NEW) LAN Installation During Normal And Outside Normal     Business Hours including VOIP Phones (Table B-2 ILI01-ILI16)
           The following Item Numbers in Table B-2 apply to Initial (NEW) LAN Installations during “Normal Business Hours”, ILI01 – ILI08.   The
           following Line Items apply to Initial (NEW) LAN Installations “Outside Normal Business Hours”, ILI09 –  ILI16.   Business  hours  are
           defined in Section C-2.1 Definitions.


           The fixed prices are provided for Initial LAN  Installations  during  normal  business  hours  and  outside  normal  business  hours.
           Installation is defined as the installation of a LAN using Government Furnished Equipment (GFE), (including all LAN connections)  and
           bringing the LAN to an Operational status.

      B-2.10      Emergency New LAN Installation During Normal – And Outside Normal Business Hours including VOIP Phones (Table B-2 ELI01-ELI16)


           The following Item Numbers in Table B-2 apply to Emergency New LAN Installation during “Normal Business Hours,” ELI01 –  ELI08.   The
           following Line Items apply to Emergency New LAN Installations “Outside Normal Business Hours,” ELI09 –  ELI16.   Business  hours  are
           defined in Section C-2.1, Definitions.


           The fixed prices are provided for EMERGENCY LAN Installations during  normal  business  hours  and  outside  normal  business  hours.
           Installation is defined as the installation of a LAN using Government Furnished Equipment (GFE), (including all LAN connections)  and
           bringing the LAN to an Operational status.



Section  C – Description/specifications/Statement of work

C-1.0 PERFORMANCE BASED STATEMENT OF WORK

      C-1.1 Introduction

           The Contractor shall provide all necessary personnel, materials, services, supplies and equipment except  that  specified  herein  as
           government–furnished to relocate Government-owned Ethernet local area networks (LAN), Voice over Internet Protocol  (VOIP)  telephony
           desktop equipment and associated peripheral equipment. This equipment is located in the  Social  Security  Administration  (SSA)  and
           Disability Determination Service (DDS) offices throughout the United States, including its territorial possessions.




      C-1.2 Background


           The Social Security Administration has approximately 2,300 local area networks located in the 10 SSA regions  throughout  the  United
           States.  These regions include the District of Columbia, Hawaii, Alaska, Puerto Rico, Guam, America Samoa, the  Virgin  Islands,  and
           the Mariana Islands.  Historically, there have been approximately 200 relocations under the current contract in  a  12-month  period.
           Most relocations are within a 50 mile radius of the proposed site.


      C-1.3       Period of Performance


           SSA is anticipating awarding contract with a base period of one-year with four (one-year) option periods plus 2  (two)  1  (one-year)
           performance based incentive periods. The total anticipated system life of the contract is seven years.


      C-1.4       Contract Minimum and Maximum Amount


            The contract minimum amount over the life of the contract, including options is $3,641,780.00. The contract maximum amount  over  the
           life of the contract, including options is $35,000,000.




C-2.0 DEFINITIONS AND REFERENCES

      C-2.1 Definitions


               2 Local Area Network (LAN) a system consisting of a set of nodes that are interconnected by a set of links.  The nodes and links
                 cover a relatively small geographic area, ranging from a few feet to a mile.  The nodes may be terminals, microcomputers,
                 minicomputers, mainframes, printers, hard disk, or workstations.  The links may be coaxial cable, twisted-pair wires, or fiber-
                 optic cable.  A typical SSA LAN will include equipment such as workstations, LAN cabinets, file servers, bridges, routers,
                 switches, patch panels, printers with stands, and etc.


               2 LAN Drops are Ethernet connections that allow equipment such as workstations, network printers, servers, switches, etc. to
                 connect directly to the network.  Note: Local Printers which are connected to workstations do not require LAN Drops only network
                 printers require LAN Drops


               2 Local Field Engineer is the first level of relocations and task support.  The Local Field Engineer assist in the deinstallation
                 and reinstallation of LAN components, not involving a file server.


               2 Local Technical Specialist is the second level of relocation and task support.  The Local Technical Specialist performs
                 reconfigurations, equipment setup, relocations involving a server.


               2 Normal business hours are Monday through Friday, the hours of 8:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m., local time.

               2 Outside normal business hours are Monday through Friday, the hours of 5:01 p.m. to 7:59 a.m., local time, including Saturday and
                 Sunday.

               2 Replacement equipment is equipment that is used to replace equipment damaged in relocation activities.  The replaced equipment
                 must be functionally equivalent to the equipment it replace.

               2 Shipping Cost is limited to the cost for pick-up, transport and delivery from the existing location to a new location (different
                 building).  Reimbursable shipping cost excludes preparation for shipping and unpacking.

               2 Successful completion and successfully completed mean that equipment and software has been restored to full operation.


               2 Voice Over Internet Protocol (VOIP) telephony desktop is the telephone instrument that is attached to a LAN cable and the
                 computer. It is a traditional phone that is on a users desk.


               2 CONUS (Continental United States) includes the 48 adjoining states, Alaska and the District of Columbia.

               2 OCONUS (Outside Continental United States) includes but not limited to Virgin Islands, Puerto Rico, Guam, America Samoa and the
                 Mariana Islands.


C-3.0 TASKS

      The Contractor must perform the following tasks:

      C-3.1 Relocation of Equipment


           The Contractor must relocate equipment as directed in a relocation order issued by the SSA COTR and as specified below:


           a)    The relocation shall consist of certificating that existing equipment is operational prior to performing the relocation  at  no
              additional cost to the Government, de-installation, packing, shipping, reinstalling of  LANs,  bringing  equipment  back  up  into
              working order and proper disposal of packing material.


           b)    The Government will give the Contractor written notice at least 30 days prior to  any  relocation  to  be  performed.   Written
              notification will consist of: the old site, new site, equipment to be moved, move start date and time, move  completion  date  and
              time, site contact and any other special requirement relating to the equipment to be moved.  The  Government  is  responsible  for
              backing up data prior to a relocation.  The Government and the Contractor may agree to a shorter lead-time upon  mutual  agreement
              of the parties.


           c)    Relocations shall be scheduled for and performed on evenings, weekends, and Federal holiday for occupied space.  For unoccupied
              space relocations may be accomplished during the week day.


           d)    The Government reserves the right to change the move dates, site relocation dates and/or time frames given to the Contractor no
              later than seven (7) calendar days prior to the move.  The Contractor may be reimbursed for actual expenses incurred as  a  direct
              result of such date/location/time-frame changes.


           e) The Contractor shall perform a “site survey” of the move at least one (1) week prior to the relocation. This  “site  survey”  will
              entail the Contractor surveying the existing space, new space, equipment to be moved, elevator access  and  loading  dock  access.
              The Contractor may also be required to meet with the Government representative for the move to discuss  move  logistics  and  time
              frames.  (Does not apply to standalone workstation relocation).  Seismic bracing is to be provided and installed by the contractor
              when required by state and local codes.  When mutually agreed upon and in lieu of site survey the Contractor must participate in a
              conference call with SSA Relocation Personnel, at least once weekly.  This  shall  be  provided  at  no  additional  cost  to  the
              Government.


           f) The Contractor shall develop and maintain a quality control report to ensure that it performs relocation activities in  accordance
              with the terms and conditions of each relocation order. All written quality control report must be  available for  the  Government
              to review and monitor anytime during the term of the contract.

           g) The Contractor shall have a sufficient number of trained technicians onsite during the site moves/relocations that  have  obtained
              Suitability Determinations in accordance with Section H-1.0 of this  contract.   The  names  of  the  technicians  performing  the
              moves/relocations shall be provided to the Government COTR 10 days prior to the work being performed via email.

           h) The Contractor shall provide a trained technician on-site the first  working  day  after  a  move  to  ensure  that  equipment  is
              operational and to handle any customer  complaints  or  perform  troubleshooting.   (Does  not  apply  to  standalone  workstation
              relocation).

           i) The Contractor shall clean up and properly dispose of all relocation associated debris immediately following a  relocation.   This
              includes removing all boxes, bubble wrap, and trash resultant from the move of equipment.

           j) The Contractor shall only employ movers, transport companies, or subcontractors that have specialized previous experience  in  the
              relocation of workstations and LAN equipment.

           k) The Contractor shall be liable to repair or replace any component damaged during relocation.

      C-3.2 Repair or Replace Damaged Equipment


           The Contractor must repair or replace damaged equipment within 24 hours of a service call from  the  SSA  Remote  Operations  Control
           Center (ROCC),


           When the contractor replaces damaged equipment the following IPV6 Internet Protocol and Section 508 requirements must be  adhered  to
           on all replacement equipment.


                C-3.2.1 IPv6 Internet Protocol


           IPv6 capability is a technical requirement for procurements of relevant network devices, system hardware and software,  applications,
           operating systems, etc.

           An IPv6 capable product or system must be able to receive, process, and transmit or forward (as appropriate) IPv6 packets and  should
           interoperate with other systems and protocols in both IPv4 and IPv6 modes of operation. Specifically, any new IP  product  or  system
           developed, acquired, or produced must:

               • Interoperate with both IPv6 and IPv4 systems and products;
               • If not initially capable, provide a migration path and commitment to upgrade to IPv6 for all application and product features by
                 June 2008; and
               • Have available IPv6 technical support for development, implementation,  and  management  of  deployed  products,  components  or
                 systems.


              C-3.2.2 Section 508 Requirements

           Requirements for accessibility based on Section 508 of the Rehabilitation Act of 1973 (29 U.S.C. 794d) and additional agency specific
           accessibility requirements, hereafter referred in total as “SSA’s Accessibility Requirements”, are determined to be relevant for this
           solicitation.  Please reference Attachment VI –SSA’s Accessibility Requirements for a specific listing of all applicable SSA
           Accessibility Requirements for all replacement equipment in accordance with Section C-3.2.




      C-3.3 Miscellaneous Relocation Tasks


           The Contractor must perform in accordance with task order issued by the CO.  The scope of this work  will  include  modifications  to
           local area networks, component installation, performing network analyses, providing advice about efficient  network  usage,  and  the
           loading of additional drivers for servers or workstations.  For tasks that involve relocations of workstations, the Contractor  shall
           certify in writing that the existing equipment is operational prior to shipment at no additional cost to the Government.


      C-3.4 Initial (New) and Emergency LAN Installations


           The Contractor shall, as directed in the task order:


               3 Install new Local Area Network (LANs) to include SSA employees into the existing Intelligent Workstation on a Local Area Network
                 (IWS/LAN) infrastructure.  These LANs will be known as “New LANs/Initial Installations.”  The Government will provide a 30-
                 calendar day written notice of intent to order an Initial Installation Order.  The Government and the Contractor may agree to a
                 shorter lead-time upon mutual agreement of the parties.
               3 Create a substitute LAN on an Emergency basis, as a replacement when the existing LAN is destroyed and renders an SSA office
                 inoperable; i.e., a fire, floor, other disaster, or in other circumstances when insufficient lead time is available.  These LANs
                 will be known as “Emergency LANs/Emergency Installations



                 (a)   Both new and emergency LANs will fit into the existing structure for  LAN  requirements  and  will  add  to  the  existing
                       platform for distributed data processing (DDP) applications within SSA.  The Government anticipates 20 new  and  emergency
                       installations per year.


                 (b)   Network Topology: The existing base of SSA LANs installed nationwide are interconnected with a  Wide  Area  Network  (WAN)
                       backbone called the SSANet.  SSANet is a star network with the central  hub  in  Baltimore,  Maryland  at  SSA’s  National
                       Computer Center, (NCC).   The Government has converted to a frame relay routed network.  SSANet  is  connected  to  remote
                       Regional Operations Control Centers (ROCCs), located in Philadelphia, PA; Jamaica, NY; Chicago, IL; Richmond,  CA;  Kansas
                       City, MO; and Birmingham, AL.  Baltimore’s NCC is also the site of a Baltimore ROCC.


                 (c)   The Government-provided network topology shall be Ethernet with cat5e or better cabling.  The Government workstations  are
                       using Windows XP operating systems or better.  All Initial Installations (new) will be done in an Ethernet topology.


                 (d)   Installation activities can occur before, during or after regular business hours, which may include weekends.   Timeframes
                       for installations work will be identified in the Installation task.


                 (e)   Access to the installation site shall be provided to the Contractor only when a designated  Government  representative  is
                       present.  In offices with public access, the Government shall make a representative available during agreed-upon hours.


                 (f)   SSA will pre-load software and current build information to the File Servers and Workstations prior to shipment to the new
                       installation.


                 (g)   Specifically the Contractor shall:

                       1)    Unpack the Government furnished equipment, (GFE), which will be shipped to the installation site by  the  Government
                         prior to the install.  The GFE will include hardware and associated software, including drivers and peripherals.


                       2)    Install, fully test and implement as operational, all equipment which can include workstations, notebook  computers,
                         peripheral devices, network servers, etc., and assure       connectivity and interoperability.


                       3)    Modify server software as required so as to make it operational; i.e., connecting to the  appropriate  ROCC  in  the
                         appropriate domain, using instructions provided by the Government.  Modify and fully test all  software  as  needed  to
                         make workstations and LANs operational, including Government-developed applications, e-mail, and personal  productivity
                         software, using instructions provided by SSA.  Upon completion of each LAN, “turnkey” use  and  operation  must  result
                         (i.e., no additional configuration should be necessary by SSA personnel or other Contractors).


                       4)   Convert workstation topology if required.


                       5)     Change network and printer identifications if required.


                       6)     Make hardware additions if required.


                       7)     Change system properties.


                       8)     Change drive mappings.


                       9)     Adhere to all SSA and industry standards.


                      10)  Provide seismic bracing where required by State or Local regulations.  This shall be provided at no additional cost to
                          the Government.


                      11)     Remove all trash from the premises of the installation site.


                      12)   Ensure that the SSA or DDS office be fully functional at the regular starting business hours on  the  Monday  morning
                          following the install or as agreed to by both   parties in the Installation Order.


                      13)    Submit one copy electronically of the completed Service Incident Report to the COTR within 5 days of the  completion
                          of each task.

C-4.0 REPORTS

      The Contractor shall prepare the following reports and submit them as specified.

      C-4.1 Service Incident Report


           Prepare a Service Incident Report immediately upon the completion of each relocation and/or task.  Sign the  report  and  obtain  the
           signature of the individual who requested the relocation or task service to indicate that  the  work  was  completed  satisfactorily.
           Leave a copy of the report with the person who requested the relocation or task and electronically submit a copy to the  COTR.   Each
           Service Incident Report shall contain the following information:

            • Date and time the service request was received,
            • Date and time of Contractor’s arrival at the service site,
            • Location of the equipment serviced,
            • LAN Drop Counts for LAN Relocations
            • Description of Relocation or task activity,
            • The date and time, that service was successfully completed.

      C-4.2   Security Screening Report


           The Contractor shall maintain an electronic file of all cleared employees and provide the COTR with copies on  a  monthly  basis  via
           email.  This report shall include all personnel who require entry onto Government Property.   When  inside  access  is  required  the
           Contractor personnel will need to be screened as indicated in Section H-1.0, Security Requirements Clause.


           The report shall include the following:


                  • Employee name (including first name, last name and middle initial)
                  • Employee SSN
                  • Employee phone number
                  • Employee email address
                  • Status of screening (ie. Pre-Approved; Final Approval)


           Note: Please refer to Section H-1.0 for the Security Requirements Clause.


C-5.0 PERFORMANCE REQUIREMENTS

      The contractor shall ensure that all work meets the performance requirements in accordance with the Acceptable Quality  Performance  Levels
      in section C-6.0 Performance Standards.


      C-5.1       Quality Control


      The contractor shall be responsible for the relocation of Government-owned Ethernet  local  area  networks  and  associated  peripheral  in
      accordance with acceptable quality performance levels.  The contractor shall re-perform work that does not meet contract requirements at no
      cost to the Government, unless otherwise directed by the Contracting Officer. Re-performance of work  shall  not  constitute  an  excusable
      cause to delay or extend any timeliness standards or deadlines. Failure to comply with  the  acceptable  quality  performance  levels  will
      affect the extension of the two (one-year) incentive periods.


      C-5.2       Quality Control Plan


      The Contractor shall develop, implement and maintain a quality control program (QCP) to ensure relocation and task services  are  performed
      in accordance with the terms and conditions of the contract. The QCP shall explain the manner in  which  the  contractor  requirements  are
      being accomplished in accordance with the contract. The contractor shall demonstrate proactive efforts to improving its services to prevent
      unsatisfactory performance from repeating and to ensure unsatisfactorily performance is addressed and rectified in  a  timely  manner.  The
      contractor shall be responsible for the quality of services provided, including those provided  by  subcontractors.  The  contractor  shall
      submit the OCP as part of the proposal. At a minimum, the Contractor shall include in the quality control plan procedures that address  the
      following areas:

           C-5.2.1  An inspection of the LAN system that enables the Contractor to identify and correct deficiencies in the quality  of  service
           before Relocation or task activities are performed and/or the Government points out the deficiencies.


           C-5.2.2 A checklist to be used in inspections.  The checklist shall include every area  of  the  Contractor’s  operations  under  the
           contract, as well as all tasks performed.


           C-5.2.3  Procedures for documenting and responding to relocations or tasks.


           C-5.2.4  A list of all inspections conducted by the Contractor, including records of  corrective  actions  taken  as  result  of  the
           inspection.


      The Contractor’s written quality control plan shall be available for the Government to review and monitor during the term of the contract.

      C-5.3       Quality Assurance Surveillance Plan

           C-5.3.1 Background

           Federal Acquisition Regulation (FAR) 37.602-2 requires that agencies  develop  quality  assurance  surveillance  plans  (QASPs)  when
           acquiring services.  These plans shall recognize the responsibility of the Contractor to carry out its  quality  control  obligations
           and shall contain measurable inspection and  acceptance  criteria  corresponding  to  the  performance  standards  contained  in  the
           performance based statement of work(PBWS).  FAR 46.401(a) stipulates that QASPs should specify (1) all  work  requiring  surveillance
           and (2) the method of surveillance.  The Government will provide the QASP to the Contractor after contract  award.   The  Contractor,
           not the Government, is responsible for management and quality control actions necessary to meet the obligations and  requirements  of
           the contract.  The role of the Government in quality assurance is to ensure that contract standards are achieved.


           The QASP has been developed to evaluate Contractor actions while implementing the PBWS of this contract.  It is designed  to  provide
           an effective surveillance method of monitoring Contractor performance for each objective of the PWS and to evaluate the services  the
           Contractor is required to furnish under this contract.  This QASP is based on the  premise  the  Government  desires  to  maintain  a
           quality standard in LAN Relocations, and Task efforts.


           In this contract, the Contractor’s Quality Control Plan is the driver for ensuring service quality.  The  Contractor  is  responsible
           for developing and following a comprehensive program of inspection and monitoring  actions  to  ensure  that  the  contract  work  is
           accomplished effectively, efficiently, and economically.  The first major step to ensuring a “self-correcting” contract is to  ensure
           that the quality control program agreed upon by the parties at the beginning of the contract provides the measures needed to lead the
           Contractor to success.  Once the quality control program is established, careful application of the methods and  standards  presented
           in the remainder of this document will ensure a robust quality assurance program.


           C-5.3.2 Performance Objectives


           The performance objectives of the performance based work statement (PBWS) and of this contract consist  of  the  following  four  (4)
           categories:


              1) Quality of Service
              2) Timeliness of Performance
              3) Business Relations
              4) Customer Satisfaction


           Contractor’s performance will be evaluated and rated based on the following:


           C-5.3.3 Surveillance Methods and Schedule


           Periodic inspections will be conducted to monitor Contractor performance.  Inspections will be conducted by  the  COTR  and/or  those
           persons the CO or COTR designate as contract Inspectors.  The Government will use any and all methods deemed necessary to ensure that
           the Contractor is in compliance with the terms and conditions of the contract.  These methods may include, but are  not  limited  to,
           periodic random inspections on services provided.  All work and services performed shall be done in accordance  with  the  terms  and
           conditions of this contract and with the Quality Control Plan.  In the event a serious deficiency  is  identified  during  a  quality
           control exercise, the CO and/or the COTR shall immediately contact the Contractor to discuss the Government’s findings and the  steps
           the Contractor will take to correct the problem(s).


           Periodically, but not less than monthly, a COTR will visit appropriate work areas serviced by the Contractor and either  observe  the
           Contractor performing the task or review documentation, as appropriate.  The COTR will notify the  Contractor’s  designated  contract
           administration representative of any performance deficiencies either immediately or at least monthly depending on the severity of the
           deficiency.  Performance deficiencies will also be subject to the terms and conditions of paragraph (a) of FAR clause 52.212-4, which
           addresses price reductions for services  not  rendered,  improperly  rendered,  and/or  for  costs  that  result  directly  from  the
           Contractor’s failure to perform.


           The COTR may also perform evaluations based upon the Contractor’s Quality Control Plan.  The COTR  may  perform  evaluations  in  any
           number of ways.  For example:


              a)  The COTR may accompany the Contractor on scheduled inspections and observe the Contractor inspecting  the  services  to  ensure
                 defects are corrected.


              b)  The COTR may immediately inspect the same area as the Contractor as soon as the Contractor has completed  the  quality  control
                 inspection to determine if any surveillance areas were overlooked.

              c) The COTR may inspect an area prior to the Contractor and compare results.  The COTR will record defects if the Contractor  fails
                 to record performance defects and defects are not corrected.

C.7.0   INCENTIVE OPTIONS

      This contract includes a base year and six (6) incentive option years.  Incentive Options are intended to reward a high level of Contractor
      performance with eligibility for additional option years.  Conversely, use of incentive options effectively prohibits the Government from
      exercising options on contracts where Contractor performance is marginal.


      The determination to award an incentive option, and the methodology used in making such determinations, are unilateral decisions made
      solely at the discretion of the Government.  The exercise of incentive options will be accomplished by unilateral contract modification, in
      accordance with Federal Acquisition Regulation (FAR) Clause 52.217-9 -- Option to Extend the Term of the Contract.


      The earned Incentive Option opportunity will be based on the Contractor’s performance during each evaluation period.  Performance
      evaluation criteria are set forth in the National Institute of Health (NIH) Contractor Performance System (CSP) using the Contractor
      Performance Insert Form – Standard Evaluation, and amplified in the table above (see Section C.6.0). If the Contracting Officer (CO) does
      not provide specific notice in writing to the Contractor of changes to the evaluation criteria prior to the start of an evaluation period,
      the same criteria from the preceding period will be used in the subsequent evaluation period.  Any changes to evaluation criteria will be
      made by revising the QASP and notifying the Contractor.


      Annual Evaluations:  The annual evaluation period concurs with the annual performance period of the contract.   Contract Inspectors will
      submit their evaluation reports to the Contracting Officer’s Technical Representative (COTR) 14 calendar days after the end of the
      evaluation period.  The COTR will reconcile the reports and document a summary report on a Contractor Performance Report – Standard
      Evaluation within 30 calendar days of the end of the performance period being evaluated.  The COTR will then forward a copy of the Report
      to the Contractor for Comment.  The Contractor has 14 calendar days to provide comments to the COTR.   When Contractor Comments are
      received, the COTR will determine the overall grade and submit the report to the CO for approval.  After CO approval, the COTR informs the
      Contractor (in writing) of its overall grade and the impact on available incentive option periods.


      Interim Evaluations:  Interim performance evaluations will be conducted when the Quarterly QASP evaluations indicate a significant decline
      in Contractor performance.  If, as a result of this review, the Contractor’s performance is determined to have fallen from Outstanding or
      Excellent to Fair or below, or from Good to Unsatisfactory,  the opportunity for all future option periods may be cancelled.  However, if
      insufficient time remains in the performance period to competitively reacquire the required services, the Government may exercise its
      unilateral right under FAR 52.217-8 to extend services for up to six months.


      One interim evaluation will be conducted at the end of the second Quarter of the base year of the contract.  The availability of the first
      incentive option period will be based on this interim evaluation.


      The following table represents the performance standards that must be met to enable the Government to exercise each incentive option.  Note
      that the performance standards grow progressively higher over the potential life of the contract. For the base year the standard is “fair”.
       The Standard for Option years #1 through #4 is “good”, and the Standard for Option years #5 through #6 is “excellent”.

|Base Year             |Best Value             |Not Applicable                                                                     |
|                      |Determination          |                                                                                   |
|Option Year #1        |FAR 17.207             |No serious performance problems in the Base year. Overall “Fair” or above interim  |

8.0  CONTRACT INSPECTORS

      Contract inspectors are subordinates of the COTR and are responsible for the day-to-day inspection and monitoring of the Contractor's work.
       The responsibility of the contract inspectors include, but are not limited to: inspecting the work to ensure compliance with the contract
      requirements; documenting through written inspection reports the results of all inspections conducted; following through to assure that all
      defects or omissions are corrected; conferring with representatives of the Contractor regarding any problems encountered in the performance
      of the work; assisting in the preparation of performance evaluations; and generally assisting the COTR in carrying out his
      responsibilities.

                 entitled, “Technical Direction.”




                       Contracting Officer’s Technical Representative:       “Given at award”


                  Alternate COTR:     “Given at award”


           (b)   The COTR, or his/her authorized representative, shall be responsible for coordinating with the Contractor the technical aspects
                 of the contract.  The COTR is not authorized to make any changes which affect the contract amount, terms or  conditions  outside
                 the scope of Section C. The Contracting Officer is the only person with the authority to act as agent of  the  Government  under
                 this contract.  Only the Contracting Officer has authority to: (1) direct or negotiate any changes in the statement of work; (2)
                 modify or extend the period of performance; (3) change the delivery schedule; or (4) otherwise change any terms  and  conditions
                 of this contract.


            G-5.1      Technical Direction

                 Performance of the work under this contract shall be subject to the technical direction of the PO or his/her designee. The term
                 "technical direction" is defined to include, without limitation, the following:



      (a)        Directions to the contractor that redirect the contract effort,     shift                 work emphasis between work areas or
tasks, require the pursuit of                certain     lines of inquiry, fill in details or otherwise serve to
accomplish contractual statements of work.


            (b)  Provision of information to the contractor that assists in the      interpretation of specifications or technical  portions  of
                 the work    description.


                 (c)    Review and, where required by contract, approve technical               reports, drawings, plans or schedules.


                 Technical direction must be within the general scope of work stated in the contract.  The PO (or designee) does not have the
                 authority to, and may not, issue any technical direction which:


                 (1) Constitutes the assignment of any additional work outside the general scope  of the contract; (2) in any manner causes an
                 increase or decrease in the total contract cost, or time required for the contract performance or (3) changes any of the
                 expressed terms, conditions or specifications of the contract.


                 All technical directions shall be issued in writing by the PO or shall be confirmed by him/her in writing within 5 working days
                 after issuance.


                 If, in the opinion of the Contractor, any instruction or direction issued by the PO is within one of the categories as defined
                 in (1) through (3) above, the Contractor shall not proceed, but shall notify the Contracting Officer, in writing, within 5
                 working days after receipt of any such instruction or direction and shall request the Contracting Officer to modify the contract
                 accordingly.  Upon receiving such notification from the Contractor, the Contracting Officer shall issue an appropriate contract
                 modification or advise the Contractor, in writing, that, in his/her opinion, the technical direction is within the scope of this
                 article.  The Contractor shall thereupon proceed immediately with the direction given.  A failure of the parties to agree upon
                 the nature of the instruction or direction, or upon the contract action to be taken with respect thereto, shall be subject to
                 the provisions of contract clause 52.212-4(d).
